/ti: ||; ti/noun [C,U] (plural T's;t's /ti:z ||; tiz/) the twentieth letter of the English alphabet 英语字母表的第二十个字母: ‘Table’ begins with (a) ‘T’. table以字母T开头。

tab
/tæb ||; tæb/noun[C]
1 a small piece of cloth, metal or paper that is fixed to the edge of sth to help you open, hold or identify it 拉环；拉手；标签: You open the tin by pulling the metal tab. 拉动金属拉环就可打开罐子。
2 the money that you owe for food, drink, etc in a bar, cafe or restaurant; the bill （于酒吧、咖啡馆或饭馆饮食应付的）费用，账款；账单
keep tabs on sb/sth(informal 非正式) to watch sb/sth carefully; to check sth 监视；监守

*table
/ˈteɪbl ||; ˈtebḷ/noun[C]
1 a piece of furniture with a flat top supported by legs 桌子；台子: a dining/bedside/coffee/kitchen table 餐桌；床头几；茶几；厨房用桌 Could you lay / set the tablefor lunch? (= put the knives, forks, plates, etc on it) 你摆餐具准备用午餐好吗？ Let me help you clear the table (= remove the dirty plates, etc at the end of a meal). 我来帮你收拾餐桌。 ☞We put things on the table but we sit at the table (= around the table). 把东西放在桌子上说put things on the table，坐在桌子旁用sit at the table。 ☞picture on page C7 见C7页插图
2 a list of facts or figures, usually arranged in rows and columns down a page 一览表: Table 3 shows the results. 表3列出结果。

*tackle¹
/ˈtækl ||; ˈtækḷ/verb
1 [T] to make an effort to deal with a difficult situation or problem 对付；处理；解决: The government must tackle the problem of rising unemployment. 政府必须处理失业人数上升的问题。 Firemen were brought in to tackle the blaze. 消防员给派来扑灭大火。
2 [I,T] (used in football, etc) to try to take the ball from sb in the other team （足球等）拦截抢球
3 [T] to stop sb running away by pulling him/her down 擒抱并摔倒（某人）
4 [T] tackle sb about sth to speak to sb about a difficult subject 与某人谈论难题: I'm going to tackle him about the money he owes me. 我要与他谈谈他欠我的钱。

*take
/teɪk ||; tek/verb [T] (past tense took /tʊk ||; tυk/ past participle taken /ˈteɪkən ||; ˈtekən/)
1 to carry or move sb/sth; to go with sb from one place to another 带；送: Take your coat with you -- it's cold. 带件外套吧。天很冷。 Could you take this letter home to your parents? 你把这封信带回家给你父母好吗？ The ambulance took him to hospital. 救护车把他送往医院。 I'm taking the children swimming this afternoon. 今天下午我带孩子去游泳。 ☞picture at borrow 见borrow插图
2 to put your hand round sth and hold it (and move it towards you) 拿；握: She held out the keys, and I took them. 她把钥匙递过来，我便接住。 He took a sweater out of the drawer. 他从抽屉中拿出一件毛衣来。 She took my hand/me by the hand. 她拉着我的手。
3 to remove sth from a place or a person, often without permission 擅自取去: Who's taken my pen? 谁拿走了我的笔？ My name had been taken off the list. 我的名字从名单上给剔除了。 The burglars took all my jewellery. 那些窃贼拿走了我的所有珠宝。
4 to accept or receive sth 接受；收到: If you take my adviceyou'll forget all about him. 你如果接受我的劝告，就会把他彻底忘掉。 Do you take credit cards? 你们接受信用卡吗？ What coins does the machine take? 这台机器接受什么样的硬币？ I'm not going to take the blame for the accident. 我不会承担这桩事故的责任。 She's not going to take the job. 她不打算接受那份工作。
5 to capture a place by force; to get control of sb/sth 攻占；控制: The state will take control of the company. 国家将接管这家公司。
6 to understand sth or react to sth in a particular way 理解为；作出某种反应: She took what he said as a compliment. 她把他的话看做是一种恭维。 I wish you would take things more seriously. 我但愿你能认真一点对待事情。
7 to get a particular feeling from sth 获得某种感受: He takes great pleasure inhis grandchildren. 他和孙儿相处感到非常愉快。 When she failed the exam she took comfort from the fact that it was only by a few marks. 她考试不及格，但令她感到安慰的是离及格只差几分。
8 to be able to deal with sth difficult or unpleasant 能应付困难或不快之事；忍受: I can't take much more of this heat. 这样炎热的天气我再也忍受不了。 [SYN] stand 同义词为stand
9 to need sth/sb 需要: It took three people to move the piano. 搬动这台钢琴需要三个人。 How long did the journey take? 这一趟路上花了多长时间？ It took a lot of courage to say that. 说出那番话需要很大的勇气。
10 to swallow sth 吞咽: Take two tabletsfour times a day. 这药片每天服四次，每次两片。 Do you take sugar in tea? 你喝茶加糖吗？
11 to write or record sth 写下；记录: She took notes during the lecture. 她上课时做了笔记。 The police officer took my name and address. 警察记下了我的名字和地址。
12 to photograph sth 拍照: I took some nice photosof the wedding. 我在婚礼上拍摄了一些精彩的照片。
13 to measure sth 量度: The doctor took my temperature/pulse/blood pressure. 医生量了我的体温╱脉搏╱血压。
14 (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时) to have a certain size of shoes or clothes 穿（某尺码的鞋子或衣服）: What size shoes do you take? 你穿几号的鞋子？
15 (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时) to have enough space for sb/sth 可容纳: How many passengers can this bus take? 这辆公共汽车可以载多少人？
16 used with nouns to say that sb is performing an action （与名词连用，表示某人的行动）: Take a look at this article (= look at it). 看看这篇文章。 We have to take a decision (= decide). 我们必须做个决定。
17 to study a subject for an exam; to do an exam （为考试）攻读（某学科）；参加（考试）: I'm taking the advanced exam this summer. 我今年夏天要参加高级程度考试。
18 take sb (for sth) to give lessons to sb （给某人）授课: Who takes you for English? (= who is your teacher) 谁教你英语课？
19 to use a form of transport; to use a particular route 搭乘（交通工具）；循（某路线）: I always take the train to York. 我去约克总是搭火车。 Which road do you take to Hove? 去霍夫你走哪条路？ Take the second turning on the right. 在第二个路口向右拐。
20 (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时) (grammar语法) to have or need a word to go with it in a sentence or other structure （在句子或其他结构中）须与某词连用: The verb ‘depend’ takes the preposition ‘on’. 动词depend须与介词on连用。
be taken with sb/sth to find sb/sth attractive or interesting 被吸引；使发生兴趣 I take it (that...) (used to show that you understand sth from a situation, even though you have not been told) I imagine; I guess; I suppose （表示理解，虽未被告知）我想，我认为: I take it that you're not coming? 我想你大概不来了？ take it from me believe me 相信我 take a lot out of sb to make sb very tired 使某人疲倦 take a lot of/some doing to need a lot of work or effort 费劲；费事；费时 For other idioms containing take, look at the entries for the nouns, adjectives, etc, for example take place is at place ¹. 其他含take的习语，参看有关名词、形容词等词条，如take place可参看词条place^1。 take sb aback to surprise or shock sb 使惊诧或震惊 take after sb (not used in the continuous tenses 不用于进行时) to look or behave like an older member of your family, especially a parent 外貌或举止像某长辈（尤其是父母） take sth apart to separate sth into the different parts it is made of 拆开；拆卸 take sth away
1 to cause a feeling, etc to disappear 使（感觉等）消失: These aspirins will take the pain away. 这些阿司匹林可以止痛。
2 to buy cooked food at a restaurant, etc and carry it out to eat somewhere else, for example at home （把餐馆等里煮好的食物）买回食用；外卖 ☞noun takeaway 名词为takeaway
take sb/sth away (from sb) to remove sb/sth （从某人处）移去，拿走，带走（某人或某物）: She took the scissors away from the child. 她把剪刀从孩子手上拿走。 take sth back
1 to return sth to the place that you got it from 退回；归还
2 to admit that sth you said was wrong 收回所说的话
take sth down
1 to remove a structure by separating it into the pieces it is made of 拆除；拆毁: They took the tent down and started the journey home. 他们拆掉帐篷，踏上归途。
2 to write down sth that is said 写下来；记录
take sb in
1 to make sb believe sth that is not true 欺骗: I was completely taken in by her story. 我完全被她的谎话欺骗了。
2 to invite sb who has no home to live with you 收留（无家可归的人）
take sth in to understand what you see, hear or read 理解，吸收（所见所闻）: There was too much in the museum to take in at one go. 博物馆收藏品内容丰富，不可能一次就全吸收消化。 take off
1 (used about an aircraft) to leave the ground and start flying （指飞机）起飞 [OPP] land 反义词为land
2 (used about an idea, a product, etc) to become successful or popular very quickly or suddenly （指理念、产品等）成功，迅速流行
take sb off to copy the way sb speaks or behaves in an amusing way （以逗笑方式）模仿 take sth off
1 to remove sth, especially clothes 脱下，除去（尤指衣物）: Come in and take your coat off. 进来，把外套脱掉。
2 to have the period of time mentioned as a holiday 休假: I'm going to take a week off. 我将休假一星期。
take on to start to employ sb 聘请；聘用: The firm is taking on new staff. 公司正在招聘新员工。 take sth on to accept a responsibility or decide to do sth 承担职责；决定做某事: He's taken on a lot of extra work. 他承担了许多额外的工作。 take sb out to go out with sb (for a social occasion) 带某人出去（参加社交活动）: I'm taking Sarah out for a meal tonight. 今晚我要带萨拉出去吃饭。 take sth out to remove sth from inside your body 除去，切除（身体某部份）: He's having two teeth taken out. 他要拔掉两颗牙齿。 take sth out (of sth) to remove sth from sth （从某处）取出，移去，除去（某物）: He took a notebook out of his pocket. 他从口袋里掏出笔记本来。 I need to take some money out of the bank. 我需要从银行里提些钱。 take it out on sb to behave badly towards sb because you are angry or upset about sth, even though it is not this person's fault 拿（某人）出气 take (sth) over to get control of sth or responsibility for sth 控制；接管；接任: The firm is being taken over by a large company. 这家商号正被一家大公司接管。 Who's going to take over as assistant when Tim leaves? 蒂姆离任后由谁接任助理一职？ take to sb/sth to start liking sb/sth 开始产生好感 take to sth/doing sth to begin doing sth regularly as a habit 开始习以为常 take sth up to start doing sth regularly (for example as a hobby) 开始爱好（某种活动）: I've taken up yoga recently. 我最近定期练瑜伽。 take up sth to use or fill an amount of time or space 使用，占用（空间或时间）: All her time is taken up looking after the new baby. 她所有时间都用来照顾刚出生的孩子。 [SYN] occupy 同义词为occupy take sb up on sth
1 to say that you disagree with sth that sb has just said, and ask him/her to explain it 质疑（某人的话）: I must take you up on that last point. 我不得不对你最后那个论点提出不同意见。
2 (informal 非正式) to accept an offer that sb has made 接受（对方的提议）
take sth up with sb to ask or complain about sth 向某人提及或提出某事: I'll take the matter up with my MP. 我会向我的议员提出这件事。

takeaway
/ˈteɪkəweɪ ||; ˈtekəˌwe/ (US 美 takeoutcarry-out) noun [C]
1 a restaurant that sells food that you can eat somewhere else 外卖餐馆
2 the food that such a restaurant sells 外卖的食物: Let's have a takeaway. 我们买一些外卖食物吧。

ˈtake-off

*talk¹
/tɔ:k ||; tɔk/verb
1 [I] talk (to/with sb) (about/of sb/sth) to say things; to speak in order to give information or to express feelings, ideas, etc 说话；谈话；表达（感情、思想等）: I could hear them talking downstairs. 我听得见他们在楼下说话。 Can I talk to you for a minute? 可以跟你谈一会儿吗？ Nick is not an easy person to talk to. 尼克可不是个好说话的人。 We need to talk about the plans for the weekend. 我们须要谈一谈周末的计划。 He's been talking of going to Rome for some time now. 他说要去罗马，已经说了好一段日子了。 Dr Hollis will be talking about Japanese Art in her lecture. 霍利斯博士上课时将讲述日本艺术。 ☞Look at the note at speak. 参看speak的注释。
2 [I,T] to discuss sth serious or important 讨论（严肃或重要的事）: We can't go on like this. We need to talk. 我们不能这样下去。我们必须谈谈。 Could we talk business after dinner? 晚餐后我们谈谈公事行吗？
3 [I] to discuss people's private lives 说闲话: His strange lifestyle started the local people talking. 他奇怪的生活方式使当地人议论纷纷。 [SYN] gossip 同义词为gossip
4 [I] to give information to sb, especially when you do not want to 提供信息，招供（尤指出于无奈）
know what you are talking about→KNOW¹ talk sense to say things that are correct or sensible 说话有道理: He's the only politician who talks any sense. 他是唯一说话还有点道理的政界人士。 talk/speak of the devil→DEVIL talk shop to talk about your work with the people you work with, outside working hours 办公时间外谈公事；三句不离本行 talk down to sb to talk to sb as if he/she is less intelligent or important than you 以高人一等的口气对人说话 talk sb into/out of doing sth to persuade sb to do/not to do sth 说服某人做╱不做某事: She tried to talk him into buying a new car. 她试图说服他买一辆新车。 talk sth over (with sb) to discuss sth with sb, especially in order to reach an agreement or make a decision 跟（某人）商议，讨论（尤指为了达成协议或作出决定）
*talk²
/tɔ:k ||; tɔk/noun
1 [C] a talk (with sb) (about sth) a conversation or discussion 交谈；讨论: Tim and I had a long talk about the problem. 蒂姆和我就那个问题谈了很长时间。
2 talks [pl] formal discussions between governments （政府间的）会谈，商讨: The Foreign Ministers of the two countries will meet for talks next week. 两国外长下星期举行会谈。 arms/pay/peace talks 军备╱工资╱和平谈判
3 [C] a talk (on sth) a formal speech on a particular subject （关于某主题的）演讲: He's giving a talk on ‘Our changing world’. 他要就“变化中的世界”这个题目发表讲话。 [SYN] lecture 同义词为lecture
4 [U] (informal 非正式) things that people say that are not based on facts or reality 空谈: He says he's going to resign but it's just talk. 他说他就要辞职，但这只是空谈而已。 ☞Look also at small talk. 另参看small talk。

*tall
/tɔ:l ||; tɔl/adj
1 (used about people or things) of more than average height; not short （指人或物）高的: a tall young man 高个子的年轻人 a tall tree/tower/chimney 高耸的树╱塔╱烟囱 [OPP] short 反义词为short
2 used to describe the height of sb/sth 有某高度的: Claire is five feet tall. 克莱尔有五英尺高。 How tall are you? 你有多高？ Nick is taller than his brother. 尼克比他弟弟高。 ☞noun height 名词为height ☞ Tall and high have similar meanings. We use tall to describe the height of people and trees (He is six foot three inches tall.) (A tall oak tree stands in the garden.) and other narrow objects (the tall skyscrapers of Manhattan). We use high to describe the measurement of sth (The fence is two metres high.)and the distance of sth from the ground (a room with high ceilings). tall和high意思相近。tall用于形容人的高度（He is six foot three inches tall.他有六英尺三英寸高。）、树的高度（A tall oak tree stands in the garden.一棵高高的橡树耸立在花园里。），以及其他狭长的东西（the tall skyscrapers of Manhattan曼哈顿高耸入云的大厦）。high用于形容事物的量度（The fence is two metres high. 栅栏有两米高。）、离开地面的距离（a room with high ceilings 天花板很高的房间）。

*taste¹
/teɪst ||; test/noun
1 [sing] the particular quality of different foods or drinks that allows you to recognize them when you put them in your mouth; flavour 味道；滋味: I don't like the taste of this coffee. 我不喜欢这种咖啡的味道。 a sweet/bitter/sour/salty taste 甜╱苦╱酸╱咸味
2 [U] the ability to recognize the flavour of food or drink 味觉: I've got such a bad cold that I seem to have lost my sense of taste. 我患了重感冒，好像吃什么都没有味道。
3 [C] [usu.sing] a taste (of sth) a small amount of sth to eat or drink that you have in order to see what it is like 少量（口尝的东西）: Have a taste of this cheese to see if you like it. 尝一尝这种干酪，看你喜欢不喜欢。
4 [sing] a short experience of sth 短暂的经历: That was my first taste of success. 这是我第一次尝到成功的滋味。
5 [U] the ability to decide if things are suitable, of good quality, etc 品味；鉴赏力: He has excellent taste in music. 他对音乐有极高的鉴赏力。
6 [sing] a taste (for sth) what a person likes or prefers 喜好；爱好: She has developed a taste for modern art. 她渐渐爱好现代艺术。
(be) in bad, poor, etc taste (used about sb's behaviour) (to be) unpleasant and not suitable （指言谈举止）失当，粗俗: Some of his comments were in very bad taste. 他的某些评论十分不得体。
*taste²
/teɪst ||; test/verb
1 linking verb taste (of sth) to have a particular flavour 有某种味道: The pudding tasted of oranges. 那布丁带有橙味。 to taste sour/sweet/delicious 吃起来味酸╱味甜╱味美
2 [T] to notice or recognize the flavour of food or drink 察觉或辨出某种味道: Can you taste the garlic in this soup? 你吃得出这汤里有蒜味吗？
3 [T] to try a small amount of food and drink; to test the flavour of sth 尝；品尝: Can I taste a piece of that cheese to see what it's like? 我可以尝一尝那块干酪，看看是什么味道吗？

ˈtaste bud
noun [C] [usu.pl] one of the small cells on your tongue that allow you to recognize the flavours of food and drink （舌头上的）味蕾

tasteful
/ˈteɪstfl ||; ˈtestfəl/adj (used especially about clothes, furniture, decorations, etc) attractive and well chosen （尤指衣服、家具、装饰等）有品味的，雅致的: tasteful furniture 雅致的家具 [OPP] tasteless 反义词为tasteless ➔tastefully /-fəli ||; -fəlɪ/ adv

tasteless
/ˈteɪstləs ||; ˈtestləs/adj
1 having little or no flavour 没味道的；平淡无味的: This sauce is rather tasteless. 这调料淡而无味。 [OPP] tasty 反义词为tasty
2 likely to offend people 可能得罪人的；不得体的: His joke about the funeral was particularly tasteless. 他那有关丧礼的笑话尤其不得体。
3 (used especially about clothes, furniture, decorations, etc) not attractive; not well chosen （尤指衣服、家具、装饰等）没有品味的，俗气的 [OPP] tasteful 反义词为tasteful

tasty

*tax

*tear²
/teə(r) ||; tɛr/verb (past tense tore /tɔ:(r) ||; tɔr/ past participle torn /tɔ:n ||; tɔrn/)
1 [I,T] to damage sth by pulling it apart or into pieces; to become damaged in this way 撕碎；撕开；给撕破 · I tore my shirt on that nail. 我的衬衫给那只钉子钩破了。 She tore the letter in half. 她把信撕成两半。 I tore a page out of my notebook. 我从笔记簿上撕下一页。 This material doesn't tear easily. 这种料子不容易撕破。
2 [T] to remove sth by pulling violently and quickly 扯下；撕掉；夺走: Paul tore the poster down from the wall. 保罗把海报从墙上撕下来。 He tore the bag out of her hands. 他从她手里夺走那个包。
3 [T] to make a hole in sth by force 弄穿；戳破
4 [I] tear along, up, down, past, etc to move very quickly in a particular direction （朝某方向）迅速移动，飞驰: An ambulance went tearing past. 一辆救护车疾驰而过。 tear noun [C]: You've got a tear in the back of your trousers. 你的裤子后面有一道裂口。
wear and tear→WEAR² tear sth apart
1 to pull sth violently into pieces 撕开；撕碎
2 to destroy sth completely 彻底破坏；毁灭: The country has been torn apart by the war. 这个国家已给战争弄得四分五裂。
tear yourself away (from sb/sth) to make yourself leave sb/sth or stop doing sth 忍痛离开（某人或某事物）；勉强停止（做某事） be torn between A and B to find it difficult to choose between two things or people 左右为难；不知如何取舍 tear sth down (used about a building) to destroy it （指建筑物）摧毁，拆掉: They tore down the old houses and built a shopping centre. 他们拆掉那些旧房子，盖了一家购物中心。 tear sth up to pull sth into pieces, especially sth made of paper 撕碎（尤指纸制品）: ‘I hate this photograph,’ she said, tearing it up. “我讨厌这张照片，”她边说边将它撕碎。

*teach
/ti:tʃ ||; titʃ/verb (past tense past participle taught /tɔ:t ||; tɔt/)
1 [I,T] teach sb (sth/to do sth);teach sth (to sb) to give sb lessons or instructions so that he/she knows how to do sth 教；讲授: My mother taught me to play the piano. 母亲教我弹钢琴。 Jeremy is teaching us how to use the computer. 杰里米教我们使用计算机。 He teaches English to foreign students. 他教外国学生英语。 I teach in a primary school. 我在小学任教。
2 [T] to make sb believe sth or behave in a certain way 训谕；教导: The story teaches us that history often repeats itself. 这个故事告诫我们历史常常重演。 My parents taught me always to tell the truth. 父母告诫我不可说谎。
3 [T] to make sb have a bad experience so that he/she is careful not to do the thing that caused it again 教训: A week in prison? That'll teach him to drink and drive! 坐一个星期牢？这是对他酒后驾车的教训！
teach sb a lesson to make sb have a bad experience so that he/she will not do the thing that caused it again 给某人一个教训

*technical
/ˈteknɪkl ||; ˈtɛknɪkḷ/adj
1 connected with the practical use of machines, methods, etc in science and industry 技术的；与科技有关的: The train was delayed owing to a technical problem. 火车因技术故障而误点了。
2 connected with the skills involved in a particular activity or subject 与某项专门或专业技能有关的: This computer magazine is too technical for me. 这本计算机杂志对我来说太专业了。

technicality
/ˌteknɪˈkæləti ||; ˌtɛknɪˈkælətɪ/noun [C] (plural technicalities) one of the details of a particular subject or activity 技术上的细节

technically
/ˈteknɪkli ||; ˈtɛknɪklɪ/adv
1 according to the exact meaning, facts, etc 从严格意义来说；根据事实: Technically, you should pay by May 1st, but it doesn't matter if it's a few days late. 严格说来，你应该在5月1日之前付款，但迟几天也没关系。
2 in a way that involves detailed knowledge of the machines, etc that are used in industry or science 科技上；技术上: The country is technically not very advanced. 那个国家技术不很先进。
3 used about sb's practical ability in a particular activity （用于指专门技能）: He's a technically brilliant dancer. 他是个技艺高超的舞蹈演员。

technician
/tekˈnɪʃn ||; tɛkˈnɪʃən/noun [C] a person whose work involves practical skills, especially in industry or science 技术人员；技师: a laboratory technician 实验室技术员

*technique
/tekˈni:k ||; tɛkˈnik/noun
1 [C] a particular way of doing sth 手段；方法；技巧: new techniques for teaching languages 新的语言教学技巧 marketing/management techniques 销售╱管理技巧
2 [U] the practical skill that sb has in a particular activity 技能；技术；技巧: He's a naturally talented runner, but he needs to work on his technique. 他天生是个有才华的赛跑选手，但他需要努力提高技巧。

ˈtelegraph pole
noun [C] a tall wooden pole that is used for supporting telephone wires 电话线杆

telemarketing
/ˈtelimɑ:kɪtɪŋ ||; ˌtɛləˈmɑrkɪtɪŋ/ =TELESALES

telepathy
/təˈlepəθi ||; təˈlɛpəθɪ/noun [U] the communication of thoughts between people's minds without using speech, writing or other normal methods 心灵感应

*telephone
/ˈtelɪfəʊn ||; ˈtɛləˌfon/ (informal 非正式phone) noun
1 [U] an electrical system for talking to sb in another place by speaking into a special piece of equipment 电话: Can I contact you by telephone ? 我打电话跟你联络好吗？ to make a phone call 打电话 What's your telephone number ? 你的电话号码是多少？
2 [C] the piece of equipment that you use when you talk to sb by telephone 电话机: Could I use your telephone? 我可以用你的电话吗？ a mobile phone (= one that you can carry around) 移动电话 a public telephone 公用电话 ☞It is more common to use phone rather than telephone, especially when you are speaking. phone较telephone常用，尤其是口语。
When you make a telephone call you first dial the number. The telephone rings and the person at the other end answers it. If he/she is already using the telephone, it is engaged. When you finish speaking you hang up or put the phone down. The number that you dial before the telephone number if you are telephoning a different area or country is called the code ‘What's the code for Spain?’ 打电话先要拨(dial)号码。电话铃响(ring)，对方接(answer)电话。对方的电话占线叫做engaged。说完话就挂断电话(hang up／put the phone down)。打外地或外国电话在拨电话号码之前先要拨地区代号，地区代号叫做code：What's the code for Spain?西班牙的地区代号是多少？ telephone(also phone) verb [I,T] Sarah phoned. She's going to be late. 萨拉打电话来说会迟一点到。 I'll phone you later. 我过一会儿给你打电话。 on the phone/telephone→PHONE

ˈtelephone box
(also phone boxˈcall box) noun [C] a small covered place in a street, etc that contains a telephone for public use 电话亭

ˈtelephone directory
(informal 非正式phone book) noun [C] a book that gives a list of the names, addresses and telephone numbers of the people in a particular area 电话簿

ˈtelephone exchange
(also exchange) noun [C] a place belonging to a telephone company where telephone lines are connected to each other 电话交换机；电话局

telesales
/ˈteliseɪlz ||; ˈtɛləˌselz/ (also telemarketing) noun [U] a method of selling things by telephone 电话销售；电话售货: He works in telesales. 他从事电话售货工作。

telescope
/ˈtelɪskəʊp ||; ˈtɛləˌskop/noun [C] an instrument in the shape of a tube with special pieces of glass (lenses)inside it. You look through it to make things that are far away appear bigger and nearer. 望远镜

teletext
/ˈtelitekst ||; ˈtɛləˌtɛkst/noun [U] a service that provides news and other information in written form on television 电视文字广播；图文电视

televangelist
/ˌtelɪˈvændʒəlɪst ||; ˌtɛləˈvændʒəlɪst/noun [C] a person who appears regularly on television to try to persuade people to become Christians and to give money 电视福音布道者﹙定期在电视上劝人加入基督教及捐款的布道者﹚ ➔televangelism noun [U]

televise
/ˈtelɪvaɪz ||; ˈtɛləˌvaɪz/verb [T] to show sth on television 用电视播放、播映或播送: a televised concert 电视转播的音乐会

*television
/ˈtelɪvɪʒn ||; ˈtɛləˌvɪʒən/ (also TV(Brit 英 informal 非正式)telly) noun
1 (also television set) [C] a piece of electrical equipment in the shape of a box. It has a glass screen which shows programmes with moving pictures and sounds 电视机: to turn the television on/off 开╱关电视机 ☞picture on page C7 见C7页插图
2 [U] the programmes that are shown on a television set 电视节目；电视: Paul's watching television. 保罗在看电视。
3 [U] the electrical system and business of sending out programmes so that people can watch them on their television sets 电视广播: a television presenter/series/documentary 电视节目主持人；电视系列片；电视纪录片 cable/satellite/terrestrial/digital television 有线╱恒星╱地面╱数字电视 She works in television. 她从事电视工作。
on television being shown by television; appearing in a television programme 在电视上播放、播映或播送: What's on television tonight? 今晚有什么电视节目？

*tell
/tel ||; tɛl/verb (past tense past participle told /təʊld ||; told/)
1 [T] tell sb (sth/that...);tell sb (about sth);tell sth to sb to give information to sb by speaking or writing 告诉；告知；说: She told me her address but I've forgotten it. 她告诉过我她的地址，但我忘了。 He wrote to tell me that his mother had died. 他写信告诉我他母亲去世了。 Tell us about your holiday. 同我们说说你的假期过得怎么样。 to tell the truth/ a lie 说实话╱谎话 to tell a story 讲故事 Excuse me, could you tell me where the station is? 劳驾，请问车站在哪里？ He tells that story to everyone he sees. 他把那个故事告诉他所见到的每个人。 ☞Look at the note at say. 参看say的注释。
2 [T] tell sb to do sth to order or advise sb to do sth 叫；命令；劝告: The policewoman told us to get out of the car. 那个女警察叫我们下车。
3 [I,T] to know, see or judge (sth) correctly 准确知道、看出或判断 [I] ‘What do you think Jenny will do next?’ ‘ It's hard to tell.’ “你认为珍妮下一步会做什么？”“很难说。” I could tell that he had enjoyed the evening. 我看得出来，他那天晚上玩得很开心。 You can never tell what he's going to say next. 没法预料他接下来会说什么。 I can't tell the difference between Dan's sisters. 丹的几个姐妹我分辨不清楚。
4 [T] (used about a thing) to give information to sb （指事物）提供数据: This book will tell you all you need to know. 本书包括一切你需要的数据。
5 [I] to not keep a secret 泄密: Promise you won't tell! 你要保证不说出去！
6 [I] tell (on sb/sth) to have a noticeable effect 有显著影响: I can't run as fast as I could -- my age is beginning to tell! 我没以前跑得那么快了─岁月不饶人哪！
all told with everybody or everything counted and included 总共 (I'll) tell you what(informal 非正式) used to introduce a suggestion （用于提出建议）你听我说: I'll tell you what -- let's ask Diane to take us. 你听我说─我们请黛安娜把我们带去。 I told you (so)(informal 非正式) I warned you that this would happen 我早就警告过你会发生这情况 tell A and B apart→APART tell the time to read the time from a clock or watch 看（钟表上的）时间 tell sb off (for sth/for doing sth) to speak to sb angrily because he/she has done sth wrong 斥责；责备: The teacher told me off for not doing my homework. 老师因我不做家庭作业而责备我。 tell on sb to tell a parent, teacher, etc about sth bad that sb has done 告发；告密

teller
/ˈtelə(r) ||; ˈtɛlɚ/noun [C] a person who works in a bank and whose job is to receive and pay out money ﹙银行的﹚出纳，出纳员

telling
/ˈtelɪŋ ||; ˈtɛlɪŋ/adj
1 showing, without intending to, what sb/sth is really like 无意中泄露实情的: The number of homeless people is a telling comment on today's society. 无家可归的人的数量是对当今社会的真实评说。
2 having a great effect 有力的；显著的: That's quite a telling argument. 那是个相当有力的论点。

ˈtell-tale
adj giving information about sth secret or private 揭秘的；泄露内情的: He said he was fine, but there were tell-tale signs of worry on his face. 他说他挺好，但他脸上露出担忧的神色。

/temp ||; tɛmp/noun [C] (informal 非正式) a temporary employee, especially in an office, who works somewhere for a short period of time when sb else is ill or on holiday 临时员工（尤指办公室人员） temp verb [I]

temper
/ˈtempə(r) ||; ˈtɛmpɚ/noun
1 [C,U] if you have a temper you get angry very easily 易怒的性情；脾气: Be careful of Paul. He's got quite a temper! 小心保罗，他脾气很大！ You must learn to control your temper. 你必须学会控制你的脾气。
2 [C] the way you are feeling at a particular time 心情；情绪: It's no use talking to him when he's in a bad temper. 他在气头上的时候你跟他说话不管用。 [SYN] mood 同义词为mood
in a temper feeling very angry and not controlling your behaviour 发怒 keep/lose your temper to stay calm/to become angry 捺住性子；发脾气 ☞Look at bad-tempered. 参看bad-tempered。

temperament
/ˈtemprəmənt ||; ˈtɛmprəmənt/noun [C,U] a person's character, especially as it affects the way he/she behaves and feels 脾气；性情；气质: to have an artistic/a fiery/a calm temperament 有艺术气质；性情暴烈；性情温和

temperamental
/ˌtemprəˈmentl ||; ˌtɛmprəˈmɛntḷ/adj often and suddenly changing the way you behave or feel 喜怒无常的；情绪容易波动的

temperate
/ˈtempərət ||; ˈtɛmpərɪt/adj (used about a climate) not very hot and not very cold （指气候）温和的

*temperature
/ˈtemprətʃə(r)/noun
1 [C,U] how hot or cold sth is 温度；气温: Heat the oven to a temperature of 200°C. 把烤箱加热到200摄氏度。 a high/low temperature 高╱低温 an increase in temperature 温度升高
2 [C] how hot or cold a person's body is 体温
have a temperature (used about a person) to be hotter than normal because you are ill （指人）发烧，发热 take sb's temperature to measure the temperature of sb's body with a special instrument (a thermometer) 量体温

template
/ˈtempleɪt ||; ˈtɛmplɪt/noun[C]
1 a shape cut out of a hard material, used as a model for producing exactly the same shape many times in another material （用于生产同类型物品的）模板，样板
2 a thing that is used as a model for producing other similar examples （用于制作类似物品的）模板，标准框，样式: If you need to write a lot of similar letters, set up a template on your computer. 如果要写很多类似的信，就在计算机上制作一块模板。

/ˈtempl ||; ˈtɛmpḷ/noun[C]

*temporary
/ˈtemprəri; US -pərerɪ ||; ˈtɛmpəˌrɛrɪ/adj lasting for a short time; not permanent 临时的；暂时的: a temporary job 临时性工作 This arrangement is only temporary. 这项安排只是暂时的。 ➔temporarily /ˈtemprərəli; US ˌtempəˈrerəlɪ ||; ˌtɛmpəˈrɛrəlɪ/ adv

*tempt
/tempt ||; tɛmpt/verb [T] tempt sb (into sth/into doing sth);tempt sb (to do sth) to try to persuade or attract sb to do sth, even if it is wrong 引诱；诱惑；勾引: His dream of riches had tempted him into a life of crime. 他的发财梦诱使他踏上犯罪的道路。 She was tempted to stay in bed all morning. 她整个早上赖在床上不肯起来。

temptation
/tempˈteɪʃn ||; tɛmpˈteʃən/noun
1 [U] a feeling that you want to do sth, even if you know that it is wrong 诱惑；引诱: I managed to resist the temptation to tell him what I really thought. 我顶住了诱惑，没把我的真实想法告诉他。 She wanted a cigarette badly, but didn't give in to temptation. 她很想抽一支烟，但并没有屈服于诱惑。
2 [C] a thing that attracts you to do sth wrong or silly 有诱惑力的东西: All that money is certainly a big temptation. 那么多金钱的确是一大诱惑。

tempting
/ˈtemptɪŋ ||; ˈtɛmptɪŋ/adj attractive in a way that makes you want to do or have sth 有吸引力的；诱人的: a tempting offer 诱人的提议

tenancy
/ˈtenənsi ||; ˈtɛnənsɪ/noun [C,U] (plural tenancies) the use of a room, flat, building or piece of land, for which you pay rent to the owner （土地及房屋的）租赁，租用: a six-month tenancy 六个月的租赁期 It says in the tenancy agreement that you can't keep pets. 租约上规定不得养宠物。

tenant
/ˈtenənt ||; ˈtɛnənt/noun [C] a person who pays money (rent) to the owner of a room, flat, building or piece of land so that he/she can live in it or use it 房客；租户 ☞Look at landlady and landlord. 参看landlady及landlord。

*tend
/tend ||; tɛnd/verb
1 [I] tend to do sth to usually do or be sth 通常是；往往会: Women tend to live longer than men. 女性一般比男性长寿。 There tends to be a lot of heavy traffic on that road. 那条路上的交通通常非常繁忙。 My brother tends to talk a lot when he's nervous. 我哥哥一紧张就滔滔说个不停。
2 [I] used for giving your opinion in a polite way （用于有礼貌地提出意见）: I tend to think that we shouldn't interfere. 我觉得我们不应该介入。
3 [I,T] (formal 正式)tend (to) sb/sth to look after sb/sth 照顾；照料: Paramedics tended (to) the injured. 护理人员照料伤员。

tendency
/ˈtendənsi ||; ˈtɛndənsɪ/noun [C] (plural tendencies)a tendency (to do sth/towards sth) something that a person or thing usually does; a way of behaving 倾向；趋向；行为方式: They both have a tendency to be late for appointments. 他们两个人赴约往往会迟到。 The dog began to show vicious tendencies. 那只狗开始露出凶相。 She seems to have a tendency towards depression. 她似乎容易情绪消沉。

tender¹
/ˈtendə(r) ||; ˈtɛndɚ/adj
1 kind and loving 仁慈的；温柔的；亲切的: tender words/looks/kisses 亲切的话；慈祥的面容；温柔的吻
2 (used about food) soft and easy to cut or bite; not tough （指食物）嫩的: The meat should be nice and tender. 这肉应该是挺嫩的。
3 (used about a part of the body) painful when you touch it （指身体某部位）触痛的
at a tender age; at the tender age of... when still young and without much experience 年轻时；在涉世未深的年龄: She went to live in London at the tender age of 15. 她年仅15就到伦敦生活。 ➔tenderly adv ➔tenderness noun [U]
tender²
/ˈtendə(r) ||; ˈtɛndɚ/verb [I,T] (written 书面语) to offer or give sth formally 正式提出或提交 · After the scandal the Foreign Minister was forced to tender her resignation. 丑闻传出后，外交部长被逼提交辞呈。 tender(also bid) noun [C]: Several firms submitted a tender for the catering contract. 几家公司投标承接那项饮食服务合同。

*tennis

tenor
/ˈtenə(r) ||; ˈtɛnɚ/noun [C] a fairly high singing voice for a man; a man with this voice 男高音（歌手）: Pavarotti is a famous Italian tenor. 帕瓦罗蒂是著名的意大利男高音歌唱家。 Tenor is between alto and baritone. 男高音介于男声最高音(alto)和男中音(baritone)之间。 tenor adj (only before a noun 只用于名词前) a tenor saxophone/trombone 次中音萨克斯管╱长号

*tense¹
/tens ||; tɛns/adj
1 (used about a person) not able to relax because you are worried or nervous （指人）紧张的，焦虑的: She looked pale and tense. 她看来又苍白又紧张。
2 (used about a muscle or a part of the body) tight; not relaxed （指人的肌肉或某部位）紧绷的
3 (used about an atmosphere or a situation) in which people feel worried and not relaxed （指气氛或处境）紧张的，担心的

tension
/ˈtenʃn ||; ˈtɛnʃən/noun
1 [U] the condition of not being able to relax because you are worried or nervous 紧张（状态）: I could hear the tension in her voice as she spoke. 从她说话的声音，我感觉到她很紧张。
2 [C,U] bad feeling and lack of trust between people, countries, etc （人、国家等之间的）紧张关系或局势: There are signs of growing tensions between the two countries. 有迹象表明那两个国家的关系日趋紧张。
3 [U] (used about a rope, muscle, etc) the state of being stretched tight; how tightly sth is stretched （指绳索、肌肉等）紧张的状态或程度；拉力；张力: The massage relieved the tension in my neck. 按摩消除了我脖子僵硬的感觉。

*tent

/ˈtenjə(r);-ʒər ||; ˈtɛnjɚ; ɝɛḷɛTɛ/noun [U] a legal right to live in a place, hold a job, use land, etc for a certain time （房地产的）保有权；（职务的）任期

*term¹
/tɜ:m ||; tɝm/noun
1 [C] a word or group of words with a particular meaning 词语；术语；专门用语: What exactly do you mean by the term ‘racist’? 你用racist这个词的确切意义是什么？ a technical term in computing 计算机技术术语
2 terms [pl] in terms of ...;in ... terms used for showing which particular way you are thinking about sth or from which point of view （指从某方面或角度看）: The flat would be ideal in terms of size, but it is very expensive. 这公寓的面积很理想，但是价钱太贵了。
3 terms [pl] the conditions of an agreement （协议中的）规定；条款: Under the terms of the contract you must give a week's notice. 按照合约规定，你必须在一星期前发出通知。 Both sides agreed to the peace terms. 双方都接受和平条款。
4 [C] a period of time into which a school or university year is divided 学期: the autumn/spring/summer term 秋╱春╱夏季学期 an end-of-term test 期末考试
5 [C] a period of time for which sth lasts 期限；任期: The US President is now in his second term of office. 现在的美国总统是第二届连任。
be on equal terms (with sb)→EQUAL¹ be on good, friendly, etc terms (with sb) to have a friendly relationship with sb （与某人）关系好，友好 come to terms with sth to accept sth unpleasant or difficult 屈从；妥协；让步 in the long/short term over a long/short period of time in the future 长远╱短期而言
*term²
/tɜ:m ||; tɝm/verb [T] to describe sb/sth by using a particular word or expression 把…称为: the period of history that is often termed the ‘Dark Ages’ 经常被称为“黑暗时代”的那段历史时期

terminal¹
/ˈtɜ:mɪnl ||; ˈtɝmənḷ/adj (used about an illness) slowly causing death （指疾病）晚期的，末期的: terminal cancer 晚期癌症 ➔terminally /-nəli ||; -nḷɪ/ adv a terminally ill patient 晚期病人
terminal²
/ˈtɜ:mɪnl ||; ˈtɝmənḷ/noun[C]
1 a large railway station, bus station or building at an airport where journeys begin and end （铁路、公共汽车的）终点站，总站；候机楼；航站: the bus terminal 公共汽车总站 Which terminal are you flying from? 你从哪个航站起飞？
2 the computer that one person uses for getting information from a central computer or for putting information into it （计算机的）终端

terminate
/ˈtɜ:mɪneɪt ||; ˈtɝməˌnet/verb [I,T] (formal 正式) to end or to make sth end 结束；终止 [T] to terminate a contract/an agreement 终止合约╱协议 ➔termination noun [U]

terminology
/ˌtɜ:mɪˈnɒlədʒi ||; ˌtɝməˈnɑlədʒɪ/noun [U] the special words and expressions that are used in a particular profession, subject or activity 专门用语；术语

terminus
/ˈtɜ:mɪnəs ||; ˈtɝmənəs/noun [C] (plural terminuses /-nəsɪz ||; -nəsɪz/) the last stop or station at the end of a bus route or railway line （铁路或公共汽车路线的）终点站

termite
/ˈtɜ:maɪt ||; ˈtɝmaɪt/noun [C] a small insect that lives in large groups, mainly in hot countries. Termites eat the wood of trees and buildings. 白蚁

terrace
/ˈterəs ||; ˈtɛrəs/noun
1 [C] a flat area of stone next to a restaurant or large house where people can have meals, sit in the sun, etc 平台；露台 ☞Look at patio, veranda and balcony. 参看patio、veranda及balcony。
2 (Brit 英) [C] a line of similar houses that are all joined together 排屋（外表结构相似的一排房屋）；联立房屋
3 [C] [usu.pl] one of a series of steps that are cut into the side of a hill so that crops can be grown there 梯田 ☞picture at flood plain 见flood plain插图
4 terraces [pl] the wide steps that people stand on to watch a football match （供观众站立观看足球比赛的）露天阶梯看台

terraced
/ˈterəst ||; ˈtɛrəst/adj
1 (Brit 英) (used about a house) forming part of a line of similar houses that are all joined together （指房屋）并列成排的
2 (used about a hill) having steps cut out of it so that crops can be grown there （指山）台阶形的，梯田状的

terracotta
/ˌterəˈkɒtə ||; ˈtɛrəˈkɑtə/noun [U] reddish-brown clay that has been baked but not covered in a shiny transparent substance(glaze), and is used for making pots, etc 赤陶土（已烧过，但未上釉，用于制罐等）

terrain
/təˈreɪn ||; tɛˈren/noun [U] land of the type mentioned 地形；地势: mountainous/steep/rocky terrain 多山╱陡峭╱多岩石的地势

terrestrial
/təˈrestriəl ||; təˈrɛstrɪəl/adj
1 (technical 术语) (used about animals and plants) living on the land or on the ground, rather than in water, in trees or in the air ﹙动植物﹚陆地的，陆栖的，陆生的: terrestrial species/animals/plants 陆生物种/动物/植物 a terrestrial habitat 陆上栖息地
2 connected with the planet Earth 地球的；地球上的: terrestrial life 地球上的生物 ☞ Compare extraterrestrial. 与 extraterrestrial 比较。
3 (used about television and broadcasting systems) operating on earth rather than from a satellite ﹙电视和广播系统﹚陆地上的，地面上的

*terrible
/ˈterəbl ||; ˈtɛrəbḷ/adj
1 very unpleasant; causing great shock or injury 可怕的: a terrible accident 严重的事故 terrible news 可怕的消息 What a terrible thing to do! 怎么可以做这么可怕的事！
2 ill or very upset 生病的；不舒服的；非常难过的: I feel terrible. I think I'm going to be sick. 我很不舒服，我想快要呕吐了。 He felt terrible when he realized what he had done. 他知道自己做的是什么事后，觉得很难过。
3 very bad; of poor quality 糟糕的；差劲的: a terrible hotel/book/memory/driver 差劲的旅馆╱书╱记性╱司机
4 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) used to emphasize how bad sth is （用于强调不好的程度）剧烈的，厉害的: in terrible pain/trouble 疼得厉害；处境狼狈不堪 The room was in a terrible mess. 这房间凌乱不堪。

*terribly
/ˈterəbli ||; ˈtɛrəblɪ/adv
1 very 非常；很: I'm terribly sorry. 我非常抱歉。
2 very badly 非常坏；很差: I played terribly. 我演奏得很差。 The experiment went terribly wrong. 实验出了大问题。

terrier
/ˈteriə(r) ||; ˈtɛrɪɚ/noun [C] a type of small dog 

terrific
/təˈrɪfɪk ||; təˈrɪfɪk/adj
1 (informal 非正式) extremely nice or good; excellent 极好的；绝佳的；很棒的: You're doing a terrific job! 你做得棒极了！
2 (only before a noun 只用于名词前) very great 巨大的；极度的: I've got a terrific amount of work to do. 我有一大堆事要做。 ➔terrifically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv terrifically expensive 非常昂贵

*terrified
/ˈterɪfaɪd ||; ˈtɛrəˌfaɪd/adj terrified (of sb/sth) very afraid 非常害怕的；恐惧的: I'm absolutely terrified of snakes. 我对蛇怕得要命。 What's the matter? You look terrified. 怎么回事？你看样子给吓坏了。

territorial
/ˌterəˈtɔ:riəl ||; ˌtɛrəˈtɔrɪəl/adj (onlybeforea noun 只用于名词前) connected with the land or area of sea that belongs to a country 与领土或领海有关的

territory
/ˈterətri; US -tɔ:rɪ ||; ˈtɛrəˌtɔrɪ/noun (plural territories)
1 [C,U] an area of land that belongs to one country 领土；版图: to fly over enemy territory 飞越敌人领土上空
2 [C,U] an area that an animal has as its own （动物的）地盘
3 [U] an area of knowledge or responsibility （知识、职责的）范围，领域: Computer programming is Frank's territory. 计算机程序设计是弗兰克的职责范围。

terror
/ˈterə(r) ||; ˈtɛrɚ/noun
1 [U] very great fear 恐怖；惊恐；恐惧: He screamed in terror as the rats came towards him. 老鼠向他窜过来的时候，他吓得尖叫起来。
2 [C] a person or thing that makes you feel afraid 令人惊恐的人或物: the terrors of the night 黑夜的恐怖
3 [U] violence and the killing of ordinary people for political purposes （有政治目的的）暴力活动，恐怖行为: a campaign of terror 一系列恐怖活动
4 [C] a person or animal, especially a child, that is difficult to control 难以对付的人或动物（尤指儿童）: Joey's a little terror. 乔伊是个小捣蛋。

terrorism
/ˈterərɪzəm ||; ˈtɛrəˌrɪzəm/noun [U] the killing of ordinary people for political purposes 恐怖主义；恐怖活动: an act of terrorism 恐怖行动 ➔terrorist /ˈterərɪst ||; ˈtɛrərɪst/ noun [C]: adj

terrorize
/ˈterəraɪz ||; ˈtɛrəˌraɪz/ (also -ise) verb [T] to make sb feel frightened by using or threatening to use violence against him/her 恐吓；威胁: The gang has terrorized the neighbourhood for months. 数月来，那个帮派已使那一带的人惶惶不可终日。

*test¹
/test ||; tɛst/noun[C]
1 a short exam to measure sb's knowledge or skill in sth 测验: We have a spelling test every Friday. 我们每星期五有拼写测验。 When you take a test you can either pass it (succeed) or fail it (not succeed). 参加测验(take a test)及格叫做pass，不及格叫做fail。
2 a short medical examination of a part of your body （身体某部位的）检查，化验: to have an eye test 检查眼睛
3 an experiment to find out if sth works or to find out more information about it 测试: Tests show that the new drug is safe and effective. 测试结果显示新药安全有效。 to carry out/perform/do a test 完成╱进行╱做测试
4 a situation or an event that shows how good, strong, etc sb/sth is 试验；测试；考验；试金石
put sb/sth to the test to do sth to find out how good, strong, etc sb/sth is 使经受考验；检验；测试
*test²
/test ||; tɛst/verb[T]
1 test sb/sth (for sth);test sth (on sb/sth) to try, use or examine sth carefully to find out if it is working properly or what it is like 测试；试验: These cars have all been tested for safety. 这些汽车全部经过安全测试。 Do you think drugs should be tested on animals? 你认为应该对动物进行药物试验吗？
2 to examine a part of the body to find out if it is healthy 检查（身体）: to have your eyes tested 检查眼睛
3 test sb (on sth) to examine sb's knowledge or skill in sth 测试（某人的知识或技术）: We're being tested on irregular verbs this morning. 我们今天上午要进行不规则动词测验。

*text¹

2 [C] the written form of a speech, INTERVIEW, etc （演说、采访等的）原文，讲稿: The newspaper printed the complete text of the interview. 报章刊载了这次采访的全文。

*than
/ðən;strong form ðæn ||; ðən; ðæn/ conj prep
1 used when you are comparing two things （作比较时用）比，较: He's taller than me. 他个子比我高。 He's taller than I am. 他个子比我高。 London is more expensive than Madrid. 伦敦的物价比马德里的高。 You speak French much better than she does/than her. 你的法语说得比她好多了。
2 used with ‘more’ and ‘less’ before numbers, expressions of time, distance, etc （放在数字或表示时间、距离等的词语前，与more或less连用）: I've worked here for more than three years. 我在这里工作已经三年多了。
3 used after ‘would rather’ to say that you prefer one thing to another （放在would rather后，表示比较偏好某事物）: I'd rather play tennis than football. 与踢足球相比，我比较喜欢打网球。

*thank
/θæŋk ||; θæŋk/verb [T] thank sb (for sth/for doing sth) to tell sb that you are grateful 感谢；谢谢；道谢；致谢: I'm writing to thank you for the present you sent me. 收到你送给我的礼物，谨此专函致谢。 I'll go and thank him for offering to help. 他主动帮助我，我要去向他道谢。 ☞ Thank you and thanks are both used for telling somebody that you are grateful for something. Thanks is more informal Thank you very much for your letter. ‘How are you, Rachel?’ ‘Much better, thanks.’ You can also use thank you and thanks to accept something that somebody has offered to you ‘Stay for dinner.’ ‘Thank you. That would be nice.’ When you want to refuse something you can say no, thank you or no, thanks ‘Would you like some more tea?’ ‘No, thanks.’ 表示谢意可以用thank you或thanks。thanks用于非正式的场合：Thank you very much for your letter.收到你的信，十分感谢。·‘How are you, Rachel?’ ‘Much better, thanks.’“雷切尔，身体好吗？”“好多了，谢谢。”表示接纳对方给你的东西亦可以说thank you或thanks：‘Stay for dinner.’ ‘Thank you. That would be nice.’“留下吃晚饭吧。”“好的，谢谢。”婉言拒绝对方的提议可以说no, thank you或no, thanks：‘Would you like some more tea?’ ‘No, thanks.’“你还要茶吗？”“不用了，谢谢。” thank God/goodness/heavens used for expressing happiness that sth unpleasant has stopped or will not happen （用于表示放下心来或松一口气）感谢上帝，谢天谢地: Thank goodness it's stopped raining. 谢天谢地，雨总算停了。

thankful
/ˈθæŋkfl ||; ˈθæŋkfəl/adj thankful (for sth/to do sth/that...) (not before a noun 不用于名词前) pleased and grateful 高兴；感激: I was thankful to hear that you got home safely. 听到你平安到家的消息，我很高兴。 I was thankful for my thick coat when it started to snow. 天开始下雪时，我真高兴有一件厚外套。

thankfully
/ˈθæŋkfəli/adv
1 used for expressing happiness that sth unpleasant did not or will not happen （用于表示放下心来或舒一口气） [SYN] fortunately 同义词为fortunately Thankfully, no one was injured in the accident. 谢天谢地，这次事故没有人受伤。
2 in a pleased or grateful way 高兴地；感激地: I accepted her offer thankfully. 我满怀感激接受了她的提议。

thankless
/ˈθæŋkləs ||; ˈθæŋklɪs/adj involving hard work that other people do not notice or thank you for 吃力不讨好的

*thanks
/θæŋks ||; θæŋks/noun [pl] words which show that you are grateful （表示感谢的用语）谢谢: I'd like to express my thanks to all of you for coming here today. 我衷心感谢各位今天光临。 thanks to sb/sth because of sb/sth 由于；因为: We're late, thanks to you! 因为你的缘故，我们才迟到！ a vote of thanks→VOTE¹

Thanksgiving (Day)
/ˌθæŋksˈgɪvɪŋ deɪ ||; ˌθæŋksˈgɪvɪŋ ˌde/noun [U] [C] a public holiday in the US and in Canada 感恩节 Thanksgiving Day is on the fourth Thursday in November in the US and on the second Monday in October in Canada. It was originally a day when people thanked God for the harvest. 美国的感恩节在十一月份的第四个星期四，加拿大的在十月份的第二个星期一，本都是感谢上帝赐予收成的日子。

ˈthank you
noun [C] an expression of thanks 感谢；致谢

*that
/ðæt ||; ðæt/det pronoun conj adv
1 (plural those /ðəʊz ||; ðoz/) used to refer to a person or thing, especially when he/she/it is not near the person speaking （用于指人或事物，尤指较远的）那个: I like that house over there. 我喜欢那边那幢房子。 What's that in the road? 路上那个东西是什么？ ‘Could you pass me the book?’ ‘This one?’ ‘No, that one over there.’ “可以把书递给我吗？”“这本吗？”“不，那边那本。”
2 (plural those /ðəʊz ||; ðoz/) used for talking about a person or thing already known or mentioned （用于指已知或已提及的人或事物）那: That was the year we went to Spain, wasn't it? 就是我们去西班牙那一年，是不是？ Can you give me back that money I lent you last week? 把上星期我借给你的钱还给我好吗？
3 /ðət ;strong form ðæt ||; ðət; ðæt/ (used for introducing a relative clause 用于引出关系从句) the person or thing already mentioned 提过的人或事物: I'm reading the book that won the Booker prize. 我正在看一本赢得布克小说奖的书。 The people that live next door are French. 隔壁住的是法国人。
When that is the object of the verb in the relative clause, it is often left out I want to see the doctor (that) I saw last week. I wore the dress (that) I bought in Paris. 作关系从句的宾语时，that常省略：I want to see the doctor (that) I saw last week.我想见我上星期见过的医生。· I wore the dress (that) I bought in Paris.我穿上在巴黎购买的连衣裙。
4 /ðət ;strong form ðæt ||; ðət; ðæt/ used after certain verbs, nouns and adjectives to introduce a new part of the sentence （用于某些动词、名词和形容词后，以引出句子的另一部份）: She told me that she was leaving. 她告诉我她要走了。 I hope that you feel better soon. 我希望你很快就好转。 I'm certain that he will come. 我肯定他会来。 It's funny that you should say that. 你居然会那么说，真好笑。
That is often left out in this type of sentence I thought you would like it. 在这类型句子中，that通常被省略：I thought you would like it.我还以为你会喜欢。
5 (used with adjectives, adverbs) as much as that （与形容词、副词连用）那么: 30 miles? I can't walk that far. 30英里？我走不了那么远。
that is (to say) used when you are giving more information about sb/sth （作补充时用）也就是说: I'm on holiday next week. That's to say, from Tuesday. 我下星期放假，也就是说，从星期二开始。 that's that there is nothing more to say or do （没什么要多说或多做）就这样: I'm not going and that's that. 我不去，就这样。

thatched
/θætʃt ||; θætʃt/adj (used about a building) having a roof made of dried grass (straw) or a similar material （指建筑物）茅草屋顶的

thaw
/θɔ: ||; θɔ/verb [I,T] thaw (sth) (out) to become or to make sth become soft or liquid again after freezing 解冻；融化: Is the snow thawing? 雪正在融化吗？ Always thaw chicken thoroughly before you cook it. 总要把鸡完全解冻后才好烹调。 ☞Look at melt. 参看melt。 thaw noun [C] [usu.sing]

*the
/ðə;ði;strong form ði: ||; ðə; ðɪ; ði/definite article
1 used for talking about a person or thing that is already known or that has already been mentioned （指已知或提过的人或事物）: I took the children to the dentist. 我带这些孩子去看牙医。 We met the man who bought your house. 我们遇见买了你房子的人。 The milk is in the fridge. 牛奶在冰箱里。
2 used when there is only one of sth （指唯一的事物时用）: The sun is very strong today. 今天阳光很强烈。 Who won the World Cup? 哪个队赢了世界杯足球赛？ the government 政府
3 used with numbers and dates （与数字和日期连用）: This is the third time I've seen this film. 这是我第三次看这部影片。 Friday the thirteenth 十三日星期五 I grew up in the sixties. 我在六十年代长大。
4 used with adjectives to name a group of people （与形容词连用，指属同一类别的人）: the French 法国人 the poor 穷人
5 (formal 正式) used with a SINGULAR noun when you are talking generally about sth （与单数名词连用，泛指某事物）: The dolphin is an intelligent animal. 海豚是聪明的动物。
6 with units of measurement, meaning ‘every’ （与度量衡单位连用，表示“每”的意思）: Our car does forty miles to the gallon. 我们的汽车每加仑汽油可走四十英里。
7 with musical instruments （与乐器连用）: Do you play the piano? 你会弹钢琴吗？
8 the well-known or important one 最著名或重要: ‘My best friend at school was Tony Blair.’ ‘You mean the Tony Blair?’ “我在学校里最要好的朋友是托尼˙布莱尔。”“你是说那个当首相的托尼˙布莱尔吗？” ☞‘The’ is pronounced /ði:/ in this sense. 作此义时the应读作/Di:/。
9 the... the... used for saying that the way in which two things change is connected （用于指两项事物改变的程度相等）: The more you eat, the fatter you get. 你吃得越多就越胖。 ☞For more information about articles, look at the Quick Grammar Reference section at the back of this dictionary. 有关冠词的详细用法，参看本词典末“语法便览”部份。

/ɪmˈpɜ:fɪkt ||; ɪmˈpɝfɪkt/noun [U] (grammar语法) used for expressing action in the past that is not completed 未完成时；未完成式: In ‘I was having a bath’, the verb is in the imperfect. 在I was having a bath这个句子里，动词用了未完成时。 It is more usual to call this tense the past continuous or past progressive. 未完成时一般叫做past continuous或past progressive（过去进行时）。

the ˈLabour Party
(also Labour) noun [sing] [with.sop] one of the main political parties in Britain. The Labour Party supports the interests of working people （英国的）工党: He has always voted Labour. 他总是投工党的票。 a Labour MP 工党议员 ☞ Look at the Conservative Party and the Liberal Democrats. 参看the Conservative Party及the Liberal Democrats。

the ˈLadies

the latest
noun [sing] (informal 非正式) the most recent or the newest thing or piece of news 最近或最新的东西；最新消息: This is the very latest in computer technology. 这是最新的计算机技术。 This is the latest in a series of attacks by this terrorist group. 这是这个恐怖组织一连串袭击行动的最新一次。 at the latest no later than the time or the date mentioned 至迟；最晚: You need to hand your projects in by Friday at the latest. 你至迟要在星期五把作业交给我。

the latter
noun [sing] pronoun the second (of two people or things that are mentioned) （两者之中的）后者: The options were History and Geography. I chose the latter. 选修科目是历史和地理，我选了后者。 ☞ The first of two people or things that are mentioned is the former. 两者之中的前者叫做the former。

the limelight
/ˈlaɪmlaɪt ||; ˈlaɪmˌlaɪt/noun [U] the centre of public attention 公众注意的中心: to be in/out of the limelight 引人注目；不引人注目

*them
/ðəm;strong form ðem ||; ðəm; ðɛm/pronoun (the object of a verb or preposition 动词或介词的宾语)
1 the people or things mentioned earlier （先前已提及的人或事物）他们，她们，它们: I'll phone them now. 我现在就给他们打电话。 ‘I've got the keys here.’ ‘Oh good. Give them to me.’ “我这里有钥匙。”“哦，好，给我吧。” We have students from several countries but most of them are Italian. 我们的学生来自好几个国家，但大多数是意大利人。 They asked for your address so I gave it to them. 他们要你的地址，所以我就给了他们。
2 (informal 非正式) him or her 他；她: If anyone phones, tell them I'm busy. 如果有人打电话来，就跟他（她）说我很忙。 ☞'Them' is sometimes written 'em to represent the way that it is said in informal speech. them有时写作'em，表示这话是在非正式场合说的。

thematic
/θɪˈmætɪk; US θi:- ||; θiˈmætɪk/adj connected with the subject or subjects of sth 主题的；主题目的: the thematic structure of a text 语篇的主题结构 ➔thematically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv The books have been grouped thematically. 书籍已按主题分类。

theme
/θi:m ||; θim/noun [C] the subject of a talk, a piece of writing or a work of art （谈话或写作的）主题，主旨: The theme of today's discussion will be ‘Our changing cities’. 今天的论题是“我们演变中的城市”。

*themselves
/ðəmˈselvz ||; ðəmˈsɛlvz/pronoun
1 used when the people or things who do an action are also affected by it （表示人或动物受自己行为影响）他们自己，她们自己，它们自己: Helen and Sarah seem to be enjoying themselves. 海伦和萨拉似乎玩得很快乐。 People often talk to themselves when they are worried. 感到忧虑的人往往自言自语。
2 used to emphasize ‘they’ （用于强调they）: They themselves say that the situation cannot continue. 他们自己说不能让这种情况继续下去。 Did they paint the house themselves? (= or did sb else do it for them?) 这房子是他们自己油漆的吗？
(all) by themselves
1 alone 独自: The boys are too young to go out by themselves. 那些男孩太小，不能让他们自己出去。 ☞Look at the note at alone. 参看alone的注释。
2 without help 自行；独力: The children cooked the dinner all by themselves. 孩子们自己烧了晚饭。

*then
/ðen ||; ðɛn/adv
1 (at) that time 那时；当时: In 1990? I was at university then. 1990年？我当时在大学念书。 I spoke to him on Wednesday, but I haven't seen him since then. 我星期三跟他说过话，但此后我再没有见过他。 They met in 1941 and remained close friends from then on. 他们在1941年相识，从那时起一直是亲密朋友。 I'm going tomorrow. Can you wait until then ? 我明天去，你可以等到那时吗？ Phone me tomorrow -- I will have decided by then. 明天给我打电话─到那时我会做出决定了。
2 next; after that 接着；然后: I'll have a shower and get changed, then we'll go out. 我去淋个浴，换一换衣服，然后我们就出去。 There was silence for a minute. Then he replied. 沉默一会儿后，他作出回答。
3 used to show the logical result of a statement or situation （用于表示某番话或某种情况的合理结果）: ‘I don't feel at all well.’ ‘Why don't you go to the doctor then?’ “我觉得很不舒服。”“那为什么不去看医生？” If you don't do any work then you'll fail the exam. 你如果不学习，那你考试就会不及格。
4 (spoken 口语) (used after words like now, okay, right, etc to show the beginning or end of a conversation or statement) （用于now、okay、right等词之后，表示谈话或陈述的开始或结果）: Now then, are we all ready to go? 那么，我们都准备好出发没有？ Right then, I'll see you tomorrow. 好，明天见。
then/there again→AGAIN there and then;then and there→THERE

/ˈθɪərəm ||; ˈθiərəm/noun [C] (technical术语) a rule or principle, especially in mathematics, that can be shown to be true 定理，定律（尤指数学的）: Pythagoras' theorem 毕达哥拉斯定理（勾股定理）

theoretical
/ˌθɪəˈretɪkl ||; ˌθiəˈrɛtɪkḷ/adj
1 based on ideas and principles, not on practical experience 根据理论的: A lot of university courses are still too theoretical these days. 现在许多大学的课程仍然太偏重理论。
2 that may possibly exist or happen, although it is unlikely 有可能存在或发生的（虽然不大会）: There is a theoretical possibility that the world will end tomorrow. 从理论上说，世界存在明天就毁灭的可能性。 ☞Look at practical. 参看practical。 ➔theoretically /-kli ||; -klɪ/ adv

theorist
/ˈθɪərɪst ||; ˈθiərɪst/ (also theoretician /ˌθɪərəˈtɪʃn ||; ˌθɪərəˈtɪʃən/) noun [C] a person who develops ideas and principles about a particular subject in order to explain why things happen or exist 理论家

*theory
/ˈθɪəri ||; ˈθɪərɪ/noun (plural theories)
1 [C] an idea or set of ideas that tries to explain sth 理论；学说: the theory about how life on earth began 关于地球上生命起源的理论
2 [U] the general idea or principles of a particular subject 理论；原理: political theory 政治理论 the theory and practice of language teaching 语言教学的理论与实践
3 [C] an opinion or a belief that has not been shown to be true 看法；推测；揣度
in theory as a general idea which may not be true in reality 理论上: Your plan sounds fine in theory, but I don't know if it'll work in practice. 你的计划理论上不错，但我不知道实际上是否可行。

the ˌpast ˈperfect
(also the pluperfect) noun [sing] (grammar语法) the tense of a verb that describes an action that was finished before another event happened 过去完成时；过去完成式 For more information about the past perfect, look at the Quick Grammar Reference at the back of this dictionary. 有关过去完成时的详细用法，参看本词典末“语法便览”部份。

the ˌpast ˈtense
(also the past) noun [sing] (grammar语法) the form of a verb used to describe actions in the past 过去时；过去式: The past (tense) of the verb ‘come’ is ‘came’. 动词come的过去时是came。 For more information about the past tenses, look at the Quick Grammar Reference at the back of this dictionary. 有关过去时的详细用法，参看本词典末“语法便览”部份。

the ˈpenalty area
noun [C] the marked area in front of the goal in football （足球）罚球区，禁区

the ˌperfect ˈtense
(also the perfect) noun [sing] (grammar语法) the tense of a verb that is formed with has/have/had and the past participle 完成时；完成式: ‘I've finished’ is in the present perfect tense. I've finished这个句子用的是现在完成时。 ☞For more information about the perfect tense, look at the Quick Grammar Reference section at the back of this dictionary. 有关完成时的详细用法，参看本词典末“语法便览”部份。

noun [C] the sport of jumping over a high bar with the help of a long pole 撑杆跳高

the ˌpresent ˈperfect
noun [sing] (grammar语法) the form of a verb that expresses an action done in a time period from the past to the present, formed with the present tense of have and the past participle of the verb 现在完成时；现在完成式: ‘I've finished’, ‘She hasn't arrived’ and ‘I've been studying’ are all in the present perfect. I've finished、She hasn't arrived和I've been studying这些句子用的都是现在完成时。 ☞For more information about the use of tenses, look at the Quick Grammar Reference section at the back of the dictionary. 有关时态的详细用法，参看本词典末“语法便览”部份。

the ˌpresent ˈtense
noun [C] (also the present [sing]) (grammar语法) the tense of the verb that you use when you are talking about what is happening or what exists now

therapeutic
/ˌθerəˈpju:tɪk ||; ˌθɛrəˈpjutɪk/adj

2 helping to cure an illness 有疗效的；有治疗作用的: therapeutic drugs 治疗用的药物

therapy
/ˈθerəpi ||; ˈθɛrəpɪ/noun [C,U] treatment to help or cure a mental or physical illness, usually without drugs or medical operations 治疗；疗法: to have/undergo therapy 接受治疗 ➔therapist /ˈθerəpɪst ||; ˈθɛrəpɪst/ noun [C]: a speech therapist 言语治疗师

*there
/ðeə(r) ||; ðɛr/adv pronoun
1 used as the subject of ‘be’, ‘seem’, ‘appear’, etc to say that sth exists （作be、seem、appear等的主语，表示某事物存在）: Is there a god? 神明存在吗？ There's a man at the door. 门口有个男人。 There wasn't much to eat. 当时没有多少东西可吃。 There's somebody singing outside. 外面有人在唱歌。 There seems to be a mistake here. 这里似乎出了错。
2 in, at or to that place 那里；那边；在或往那里: Could you put the table there, please? 请将桌子放在那边。 I like Milan. My husband and I met there. 我喜欢米兰，我丈夫和我在那地方相识。 Have you been to Bonn? We're going there next week. 你去过波恩吗？我们下星期要到那儿去。 Have you looked under there? 那地方的下面你找过吗？
3 used for calling attention to sth （用于唤起注意）: Oh look, there's Kate! 看，是凯特！ Hello there! Can anyone hear me? 喂！有人听到我说话吗？
4 at that point (in a conversation, story, etc) （交谈、叙述等中）在那一点: Could I interrupt you there for a minute? 关于那一点，我可以插句话吗？
5 available if needed （须要的话）可提供: Her parents are always there if she needs help. 如果她需要帮助，她父母随时准备帮助她。
be there for sb to be available to help and support sb when he/she has a problem 可提供帮助及支持（如果某人遇到问题的话）: Whenever I'm in trouble, my sister is always there for me. 无论我什么时候遇到麻烦，我的姐姐总是乐意帮忙。 then/there again→AGAIN there and then;then and there immediately; at that time and place 立即；当时当地 there you are
1 used when you give sth to sb （用于把东西交给对方时）给你: There you are. I've bought you a newspaper. 给你，我为你买了一份报纸。
2 used when you are explaining sth to sb （作解释用）: Just press the switch and there you are! 只要单击开关，就这样！

thereabouts
/ˌðeərəˈbaʊts ||; ˌðɛrəˈbaυts/ (US 美 thereabout /ˌðeərəˈbaʊt ||; ˌðɛrəˈbaυt/) adv (usually after or 通常用于or之后) somewhere near a number, time or place 接近某数目、时间或地点；约: There are 100 students, or thereabouts. 有100名学生左右。 She lives in Sydney, or thereabouts. 她住在悉尼附近。

*thick¹
/θɪk ||; θɪk/adj
1 (used about sth solid) having a large distance between its opposite sides; not thin （指固体）厚的，粗的: a thick black line 粗黑线 a thick coat/book 厚外套╱书 These walls are very thick. 这些墙很厚。
2 used for saying what the distance is between the two opposite sides of something （用于表示厚度）: The ice was six centimetres thick. 冰有六厘米厚。
3 having a lot of things close together 密集的；密布的: a thick forest 茂密的森林 thick hair 浓密的头发
4 (used about a liquid) that does not flow easily （指液体）浓的，稠的: thick cream 浓浓的奶油 This paint is too thick. 这油漆太稠。
5 (used about fog, smoke, etc) difficult to see through （指雾、烟等）浓的: There'll be a thick fog tonight. 今晚将有浓雾。 thick clouds of smoke 一团团浓烟 [OPP] for senses 1 to 5 thin 第1至5义的反义词皆为thin
6 thick (with sth) containing a lot of sth/sb close together 充满；满是: The air was thick with dust. 空气里充满灰尘。 The streets were thick with shoppers. 街上挤满购物的人。
7 (used about sb's accent) very strong （指口音）很重的
8 (informal 非正式) slow to learn or understand; stupid 理解力差的；愚钝的；笨的 thick adv Snow lay thick on the ground. 地上的雪积得很厚。 ➔thickly adv Spread the butter thickly. 涂上厚厚的一层黄油。 a thickly wooded area 茂密的林木区
have a thick skin to be not easily upset or worried by what people say about you 脸皮厚；（对别人对自己的评论）不敏感

/θɪk ||; θɪk/noun in the thick of sth in the most active or crowded part of sth; very involved in sth 在最活跃时；在最热闹处；非常投入 through thick and thin through difficult times and situations 不顾艰难险阻；在任何情形下

*thief
/θi:f ||; θif/noun [C] (plural thieves /θi:vz ||; θivz/) a person who steals things from another person 窃贼；小偷 ☞A thief is a general word for a person who steals things, usually secretly and without violence. The name of the crime is theft. A robber steals from a bank, shop, etc and often uses violence or threats. A burglar steals things by breaking into a house, shop, etc, often at night, and a shoplifter goes into a shop when it is open and takes things without paying. A mugger steals from sb in the street and uses violence or threats. Look also at the note at steal. thief泛指偷东西的人，通常不用暴力，暗中进行，所犯的盗窃罪叫做theft。robber通常在银行、商店等使用暴力或威吓的手段抢劫。burglar常在晚上破门入屋或商店等偷东西。shoplifter在商店营业时取走物品而不付款。mugger在大街上使用暴力或威吓手段抢人东西。另参看steal的注释。

*thin¹
/θɪn ||; θɪn/adj (thinner;thinnest)
1 (used about sth solid) having a small distance between the opposite sides; not thick （指固体）薄的，细的: a thin book/shirt 薄书；薄衬衫 a thin slice of meat 薄肉片
2 having very little fat on the body; not fat 瘦的；瘦削的: You need to eat more. You're too thin! 你要多吃些，你太瘦了。
Thin, skinny, slim and underweight all have a similar meaning. Thin is the most general word for describing people who have very little flesh on their bodies. Slim is used to describe people who are thin in an attractive way You're so slim! How do you do it? If you say sb is skinny, you mean that he/she is too thin and not attractive. Underweight is a much more formal word, and is often used for describing people who are too thin in a medical sense The doctor says I'm underweight. thin、skinny、slim和underweight的意思相近。thin是形容人不肥胖或肉少的笼统说法。slim指身材苗条：You're so slim! How do you do it?你的身材这么苗条！你是怎么做到的？skinny指人瘦骨嶙峋。underweight是较正式的用语，常从医学角度形容人体重不合标准：The doctor says I'm underweight.医生说我太瘦了。
3 (used about a liquid) that flows easily; not thick （指液体）稀的: a thin sauce 稀的调味汁
4 (used about mist, smoke, etc) not difficult to see through （指雾、烟等）薄的
5 having only a few people or things with a lot of space between them 稀疏的: The population is rather thin in this part of the country. 该国这一地区人口稀少。 [OPP] for senses 1, 3 and 4 thick 第 1、3 及 4义的反义词皆为thick
thin adv Don't slice the onion too thin. 别把洋葱切得太细。 ➔thinly adv thinly sliced bread 切成薄片的面包 thinly populated areas 人口稀疏的地区 thin on the ground→GROUND¹ through thick and thin→THICK² vanish, etc into thin air to disappear completely 完全消失；无影无踪 wear thin→WEAR¹
*thin²
/θɪn ||; θɪn/verb [I,T] (thinning;thinned)thin (sth) (out) to become thinner or fewer in number; to make sth thinner 越来越少；（使）越来越薄: The trees thin out towards the edge of the forest. 越接近森林边缘，树木便越少。 Thin the sauce by adding milk. 加进牛奶把调味汁弄稀。

*thing
/θɪŋ ||; θɪŋ/noun
1 [C] an object that is not named 物件；东西: What's that red thing on the table? 桌子上那红色的东西是什么？ A pen is a thing you use for writing with. 笔是用来写字的东西。 I need to get a few things at the shops. 我要到商店去买几样东西。
2 [C] a quality or state 特性；状况: There's no such thing as a ghost (= it doesn't exist). 世上没有鬼这种东西。 The best thing about my job is the way it changes all the time. 我的工作最大优点是不断变化。
3 [C] an action, event or statement 行动；事件；言辞: When I get home the first thing I do is have a cup of tea. 我回到家里第一件事是喝一杯茶。 A strange thing happened to me yesterday. 昨天我遇到一件奇事。 What a nice thing to say! 说得真好！
4 [C] a fact, subject, etc 事实；主题: He told me a few things that I didn't know before. 他告诉我一些我以前不知道的事。
5 things [pl] clothes or tools that belong to sb or are used for a particular purpose （私人的或派某种用场的）衣服，工具: I'll just go and pack my things. 我要去收拾自己的东西。 We keep all the cooking things in this cupboard. 我们把烹饪用具都放在这个碗橱里。
6 things [pl] the situation or conditions of your life 生活情况或条件: How are things with you? 你近来情况怎么样？
7 [C] used for expressing how you feel about a person or an animal （用于表达对人或动物的感受）: You've broken your finger? You poor thing! 你把指头弄破了？真可怜！
8 the thing [sing] exactly what is wanted or needed 正想要或需要的东西: That's just the thing I was looking for! 这正是我在寻找的东西！
a close shave/thing→CLOSE³ be a good thing (that) to be lucky that 幸好；幸亏: It's a good thing you remembered your umbrella. 幸好你记得带雨伞。 do your own thing to do what you want to do, independently of other people 做自己想做的事；按自己的意愿行事 first/last thing as early/late as possible 尽早╱尽量晚: I'll telephone her first thing tomorrow morning. 我明天一早便打电话给她。 I saw him last thing on Friday evening. 我星期五晚上最后见过他。 for one thing used for introducing a reason for something （用于带出理由）: I think we should go by train. For one thing it's cheaper. 我认为我们应该乘火车，理由是车费比较便宜。 have a thing about sb/sth(informal 非正式) to have strong feelings about sb/sth 对…有强烈感受 to make matters/things worse→WORSE take it/things easy→EASY²

*think
/θɪŋk ||; θɪŋk/verb (past tense past participle thought /θɔ:t ||; θɔt/)
1 [I,T] think (sth) (of/about sb/sth);think that... to have a particular idea or opinion about sth/sb; to believe 认为；相信: ‘Do you think (that) we'll win?’ ‘No, I don't think so.’ “你认为我们会赢吗？”“不，我看赢不了。” ‘Susan's coming tomorrow, isn't she?’ ‘Yes, I think so.’ “苏珊明天会来，是吗？”“是，我想她会来。” I think (that) they've moved to York but I'm not sure. 我想他们搬到约克去了，但我不太确定。 What did you think of the film? 你觉得这部影片怎么样？ What do you think about going out tonight? 今晚出去，你看怎么样？ Gary's on holiday, I think. 我想加里在休假。
2 [I] think (about sth) to use your mind to consider sth or to form connected ideas 想；思考: Think before you speak. 开口之前先要想清楚。 What are you thinking about? 你在想什么？ He had to think hard (= a lot) about the question. 他得反复思考那个问题。
3 [I] think of/about doing sth;think that... to intend or plan to do sth 打算；计划: We're thinking of moving house. 我们打算搬家。 I think I'll go for a swim. 我想我会去游泳。
4 [T] to form an idea of sth; to imagine sth 设想；想象: Just think what we could do with all that money! 想一想那么多钱我们究竟能怎么处理！
5 [I] think about/of sb to consider the feelings of sb else 考虑到（别人的感受）: She never thinks about anyone but herself. 她从不考虑别人，只顾自己。
6 [T] to remember sth; to have sth come into your mind 记得；想起: Can you think where you left the keys? 你还记得起把钥匙遗忘在哪里了吗？ I didn't think to ask him his name. 我忘了问他的名字。
7 [T] to expect sth 预计；料想: The job took longer than we thought. 那项工作比我们预料的要费时。
8 [I] to think in a particular way 以某种方式想: If you want to be successful, you have to think big. 想要成功就得雄心勃勃。 We've got to think positive. 我们得往正面想。 think noun [sing] I'm not sure. I'll have to have a think about it. 我不敢确定。我得想一想。
think better of (doing) sth to decide not to do sth; to change your mind 重新考虑后决定不做某事；经考虑后改变主意 think highly, a lot, not much, etc of sb/sth to have a good, bad, etc opinion of sb/sth 对（某人或某事物）评价很高╱不高: I didn't think much of that film. 我认为那部影片不怎么样。 think the world of sb to love and admire sb very much 极爱慕（某人） think of sth to create an idea in your imagination 想出: Who first thought of the plan? 谁先想出这个计划？ think sth out to consider carefully all the details of a plan, idea, etc 仔细考虑计划、主意等的所有细节: a well-thought-out scheme 考虑周详的计划 think sth over to consider sth carefully 仔细考虑: I'll think your offer over and let you know tomorrow. 我会仔细考虑你的提议，明天通知你。 think sth through to consider every detail of sth carefully 彻底或全面考虑: He made a bad decision because he didn't think it through. 他做了一个错误的决定，因为他考虑得不够全面。 think sth up to create sth in your mind; to invent 想出（主意等）；发明: to think up a new advertising slogan 构思新的广告用语

2 a person who thinks in a particular way 以某种方式思考的人: a quick/creative/clear thinker 思路敏捷╱有创造头脑╱思维清晰的人

/ˈθɪŋkɪŋ ||; ˈθɪŋkɪŋ/noun[U]

2 ideas or opinions about sth 意见；看法；思想: This accident will make them change their thinking on safety matters. 这起事故会改变他们对安全问题的看法。 ☞Look at wishful thinking. 参看wishful thinking。

*this
/ðɪs ||; ðɪs/det pronoun (plural these /ði:z ||; ðiz/)
1 used for talking about sb/sth that is close to you in time or space （用于指时间或空间上较近的人或事物）这，这个: Have a look at this photo. 看看这张照片。 These boots are really comfortable. My old ones weren't. 这双靴子真的很舒服，我的旧靴子可不舒服。 Is this the book you asked for? 这是你要的书吗？ These are the letters to be filed, not those over there. 这些才是要归档的信件，不是那边那些。 This chair's softer than that one, so I'll sit here. 这张椅子比那张软，所以我要坐在这里。
2 used for talking about sth that was mentioned or talked about earlier （用于指先前提过或说过的事物）: Where did you hear about this? 你从哪里听到此事？
3 used for introducing sb or showing sb sth （介绍某人或向某人展示某物时用）: This is my wife, Claudia, and these are our children, David and Vicky. 这是我妻子克劳迪娅，这是我的孩子戴维和维基。 It's easier if you do it like this. 你这么做就会容易一些。
4 (used with days of the week or periods of time) of today or the present week, year, etc 当前的（某天、星期、年等）: Are you busy this afternoon? 今天下午你忙吗？ this Friday (= the Friday of this week) 本星期五
5 (informal 非正式) (used when you are telling a story) a certain （讲故事时用）某一个: Then this woman said... 接着这个女人说… this adv The road is not usually this busy. 这条路平常没有这么多车。

*thousand
/ˈθaʊznd ||; ˈθaυzṇd/ number 1000 千；一千 Notice that you use thousand in the singular when you are talking about a number. You use thousands when you mean ‘a lot’ There were over 70000 spectators at the match. Thousands of people attended the meeting. thousand表示数字时用单数形式。解作“很多”时用thousands：There were 70000 spectators at the match.有70000多名观众观看那场比赛。·Thousands of people attended the meeting.有许多人参加那个会议。 ☞For examples of how to use numbers in sentences, look at six. *through
/θru: ||; θru/prep adv
1 from one end or side of sth to the other 穿过；通过: We drove through the centre of London. 我们开车穿过伦敦市中心。 to look through a telescope 透过望远镜观看 She cut through the rope. 她把绳子切断了。 to push through a crowd of people 从人群中挤过去
2 from the beginning to the end of sth 从头到尾: Food supplies will not last through the winter. 食物供应维持不了整个冬天。 We're halfway through the book. 这本书我们已经看了一半。 He read the letter through and handed it back. 他把信从头至尾看了一遍，然后交还给人家。
3 past a limit, stage or test 越过（限度）；通过（阶段或考试）: He lifted the rope to let us through. 他举高绳子让我们过去。 She didn't get through the first interview. 第一次面试她就没有通过。
4 because of; with the help of 因为；藉着: Errors were made through bad organization. 出错是由于组织欠佳。 David got the job through his uncle. 戴维藉叔父的帮助得到那份差事。
5 (also thru) (US 美) until, and including 直至；直到: They are staying Monday through Friday. 他们要从星期一逗留到星期五。
6 (Brit 英) connected by telephone 接通（电话）: Can you put me through to extension 5678, please? 请替我接分机5678。
be through (with sb/sth) to have finished with sb/sth （与某人或某事物）断绝关系，一刀两断

throughout
/θru:ˈaʊt ||; θruˈaυt/adv prep
1 in every part of sth 到处: The house is beautifully decorated throughout. 房子里四处都装饰得很好看。 The match can be watched live on television throughout the world. 那场比赛全世界都可以通过电视直播观看。
2 from the beginning to the end of sth 从头到尾；在整段时间: We didn't enjoy the holiday because it rained throughout. 我们假期玩得不开心，因为整段时间都在下雨。

past tense ofTHRIVE

*throw
/θrəʊ ||; θro/verb (past tense threw /θru: ||; θru/ past participle thrown /θrəʊn ||; θron/)
1 [I,T] throw (sth) (to/at sb);throw sb sth to send sth from your hand through the air by moving your hand or arm quickly 抛；掷；扔: How far can you throw? 你能掷多远？ Throw the ball to me. 把球抛给我。 Throw me the ball. 把球抛给我。 Don't throw stones at people. 别朝人扔石子。
2 [T] to put sth somewhere quickly or carelessly 随便放置；顺手一丢: He threw his bag down in a corner. 他随手将袋子扔到角落里。 She threw on a sweater and ran out of the door. 她匆匆穿上套头毛衣，奔出门去。
3 [T] to move your body or part of it quickly or suddenly 快速或突然移动（身体或身体某部位）: Jenny threw herself onto the bed and sobbed. 珍妮扑倒在床上抽抽搭搭地哭起来。 Lee threw back his head and roared with laughter. 李把头一仰，哈哈大笑。
4 [T] to cause sb to fall down quickly or violently 使跌倒: The bus braked and we were thrown to the floor. 公共汽车突然煞车，我们都跌倒了。
5 [T] to put sb in a particular (usually unpleasant) situation 使处于（通常是不快的）境地: We were thrown into confusion by the news. 我们听到这消息都慌作一团。
6 [T] (informal 非正式) to make sb feel upset, confused or surprised 使不快、困惑或惊讶: The question threw me and I didn't know what to reply. 那问题令我困惑，不知道应该怎样回答。
7 [T] to send light or shade onto sth 投射（光或影）: The tree threw a long shadow across the lawn. 那树在草坪上投下长长的影子。 throw noun [C]: It's your throw (= it's your turn to throw the dice in a board game, etc). 轮到你掷了（指在棋类等游戏中掷骰子）。 a throw of 97 metres 投出97米的成绩
throw sth away
1 (also throw sth out) to get rid of rubbish or sth that you do not want 抛弃，扔掉（某物）: I threw his letters away. 我把他的信都扔掉了。
2 to waste or not use sth useful 浪费，不用（某有用之物）: to throw away a good opportunity 错失良机
throw sth in(informal 非正式) to include sth extra without increasing the price （出售某物时）额外赠送（某物） throw sb out to force sb to leave a place 强迫某人离开；撵走某人 throw sth out
1 to decide not to accept sb's idea or suggestion 不接受（构想或建议）
2 =THROW STH AWAY(1)
throw up(informal 非正式) to vomit; to be sick 呕吐 throw sth up
1 to vomit food 呕吐
2 to produce or show sth 出示，展示（某事物）
3 to leave your job, career, studies, etc 放弃（工作、事业、学业等）

throwaway
/ˈθrəʊəweɪ ||; ˈθroəˌwe/adj (onlybeforea noun 只用于名词前)
1 used to describe sth that you say quickly without careful thought, sometimes in order to be funny 脱口而出的: a throwaway line/remark/comment 脱口而出的诗╱话╱评论
2 (used about goods, etc 指物品) produced at a low cost and intended to be thrown away as rubbish after being used 用完即丢的；一次性使用的

thru
(US 美) =THROUGH(5)

thrust¹
/θrʌst ||; θrʌst/verb [I,T] (past tense past participle thrust)
1 to push sb/sth suddenly or violently; to move quickly and suddenly in a particular direction 猛推；猛挤；突然朝某方向快速移动 · The man thrust his hands deeper into his pockets. 那个男人把双手往口袋插得更深。 She thrust past him and ran out of the room. 她从他身边挤过，奔出房间。
2 to make a sudden forward movement with a knife, etc （用刀等）猛刺，猛插
thrust sb/sth upon sb to force sb to accept or deal with sb/sth 强迫某人接受某人或某物；强迫某人与他人打交道或处理某事
thrust²
/θrʌst ||; θrʌst/noun
1 the thrust [sing] the main part or point of an argument, policy, etc （论点、政策等的）主要部份，要旨
2 [C] a sudden strong movement forward 猛然往前移动；猛推；猛挤

thud
/θʌd ||; θʌd/noun [C] the low sound that is made when a heavy object hits sth else 重物坠地的声响；砰的一声: Her head hit the floor with a dull thud. 她的脑袋砰的一声叩在地板上。 thud verb [I] (thudding;thudded)

thug
/θʌg ||; θʌg/noun [C] a violent person who may harm other people 暴徒；恶棍

*thumb¹
/θʌm ||; θʌm/noun[C]

2 the part of a glove, etc that covers your thumb(1) （手套的）拇指部份
a rule of thumb→RULE¹ stand/stick out like a sore thumb→SORE¹ the thumbs up/down a sign or an expression that shows approval/disapproval 表示赞同╱不赞同的手势或用语 under sb's thumb (used about a person) completely controlled by sb （指人）完全在某人的支配或控制之下；受制于: She's got him under her thumb. 她已将他完全控制住。
thumb²
/θʌm ||; θʌm/verb [I,T] thumb (through) sth to turn the pages of a book, etc quickly 迅速翻动（书页等） thumb a lift to hold out your thumb to cars going past, to ask sb to give you a free ride 向路过的汽车竖起大拇指要求搭便车 ☞Look at the note at hitch-hike. 参看hitch-hike的注释。

thumbtack
/ˈθʌmtæk ||; ˈθʌmˌtæk/ (US 美) =DRAWING PIN

thump
/θʌmp ||; θʌmp/verb
1 [T] to hit sb/sth hard with sth, usually your closed hand (fist) 重击（通常用拳头）: He started coughing and Jo thumped him on the back. 他咳起嗽来，乔用力拍拍他的背。
2 [I,T] to make a loud sound by hitting sth or by beating hard 发出重击声；砰砰作响: His heart was thumping with excitement. 他激动得心里砰砰直跳。 thump noun [C]

thunder¹
/ˈθʌndə(r) ||; ˈθʌndɚ/noun [U] the loud noise in the sky that you can hear when there is a storm and that usually comes after a flash of light (lightning) 雷；雷声: a clap/crash/roll of thunder 一声霹雳；雷声隆隆；一阵雷声
thunder²
/ˈθʌndə(r) ||; ˈθʌndɚ/verb[I]
1 (used with it 与it连用) to make a loud noise in the sky during a storm 打雷: The rain poured down and it started to thunder. 大雨倾盆而下，并开始打雷。
2 to make a loud deep noise like thunder 发出雷鸣般的巨响: Traffic thundered across the bridge. 车辆隆隆驶过那座桥。

thunderbolt
/ˈθʌndəbəʊlt ||; ˈθʌndɚˌbolt/noun [C] (written 书面语) a flash of LIGHTNING that comes at the same time as the noise of THUNDER and that hits sth 霹雳；雷电

thunderclap
/ˈθʌndəklæp ||; ˈθʌndɚˈklæp/noun [C] a loud crash made by THUNDER 雷声；霹雳

thunderstorm
/ˈθʌndəstɔ:m ||; ˈθʌndɚˌstɔrm/noun [C] a storm with loud noises and flashes of light in the sky (thunder)and(lightning) 雷雨；雷暴

*Thursday
/ˈθɜ:zdeɪ;-di ||; ˈθɝzde; -dɪ/noun [C,U] (abbr Thur.) (abbr Thurs.) the day of the week after Wednesday 星期四 ☞Days of the week are always written with a capital letter. For examples of how to use the days of the week, look at Monday. 表示星期几的词，开头字母要大写。有关这类词的示例，参看Monday。

thwart
/θwɔ:t ||; θwɔrt/verb [T] thwart sth;thwart sb (in sth) to stop sb doing what he/she planned to do; to prevent sth happening 阻挠，阻止，挫败（某人的计划）；防止某事发生: to thwart sb's plans/ambitions/efforts 阻挠某人的计划╱野心╱努力 She was thwarted in her attempt to gain control. 她企图取得控制权，但给挫败了。

tibia
/ˈtɪbiə ||; ˈtɪbɪə/noun [C] (technical术语) the inner and larger bone of the two bones in the lower part of the leg between your knee and foot 胫骨 [SYN]A less technical word is shin bone. 非专门的用语为shin bone。 ☞Look at fibula. 参看fibula。 ☞picture at body 见body插图

tic
/tɪk ||; tɪk/noun [C] a sudden quick movement of a muscle, especially in your face or head, that you cannot control 抽搐（尤指脸部或头部肌肉）: He has a nervous tic. 他患有神经性抽搐症。

tick¹
/tɪk ||; tɪk/verb
1 [I] (used about a clock or watch) to make regular short sounds （指钟表）发出滴答声
2 (US 美 check) [T] to put a mark (√) next to a name, an item on a list, etc to show that sth has been dealt with or chosen, or that it is correct 打钩（表示已作处理、已选定或正确）: Please tick the appropriate box. 请在适当的方框内打钩。
what makes sb/sth tick the reasons why sb behaves or sth works in the way he/she/it does （人行为的）原因；（物运作的）原理: He has a strong interest in people and what makes them tick. 他对人及其行为的原由深感兴趣。 tick away/by (used about time) to pass （指时间）过去，消逝 tick sb/sth off to put a mark (√) next to a name an item on a list, etc to show that sth has been done or sb has been dealt with 打钩（表示已经完成或处理） tick over(informal 非正式) (usually used in the continuous tenses 通常用于进行时)
1 (used about an engine) to run slowly while the vehicle is not moving （指发动机）慢转，空转
2 to keep working slowly without producing or achieving very much 进展缓慢；呆滞
tick²
/tɪk ||; tɪk/noun[C]
1 (US 美 check markcheck) a mark (√) next to an item on a list that shows that sth has been done or is correct （表示正确或已完成的）钩号，对号: Put a tick after each correct answer. 在正确的答案后面打钩。
2 (also ticking) the regular short sound that a watch or clock makes when it is working （钟表的）滴答声
3 (Brit 英) (informal 非正式) a moment 一会儿
4 a small animal with eight legs, like an insect, that bites humans and animals and sucks their blood 蜱；壁虱 ☞picture at arachnid 见arachnid插图

*ticket
/ˈtɪkɪt ||; ˈtɪkɪt/noun[C]
1 a ticket (for/to sth) a piece of paper or card that shows you have paid for a journey, or that allows you to enter a theatre, cinema, etc 票（车票、入场券等）: two tickets for the Cup Final 两张足协杯锦标赛决赛的票 a single/return ticket to London 去伦敦的单程票╱来回票 a ticket office/machine/collector 售票处；售票机；收票员 ☞Look at season ticket. 参看season ticket。
2 a piece of paper or a label in a shop that shows the price, size, etc of sth that is for sale （标明价格、尺码等的）标签 ☞picture at label 见label插图
3 an official piece of paper that you get when you have parked illegally or driven too fast telling you that you must pay money as a punishment (a fine) （违章停车或超速驾驶的）罚款单: a parking ticket 违章停车罚款单

tickle
/ˈtɪkl ||; ˈtɪkḷ/verb
1 [T] to touch sb lightly with your fingers or with sth soft so that he/she laughs （用手指或软物）搔某人使发笑: She tickled the baby's toes. 她搔婴儿的脚趾逗他笑。
2 [I,T] to produce or to have an uncomfortable feeling in a part of your body （使）痒，发痒: My nose tickles/is tickling. 我的鼻子痒痒的。 The woollen scarf tickled her neck. 那条羊毛围巾弄得她的脖子发痒。
3 [T] (informal 非正式) to amuse and interest sb 逗人开心: That joke really tickled me. 我觉得那笑话可真逗的。 tickle noun [C]

ticklish
/ˈtɪklɪʃ ||; ˈtɪklɪʃ/adj if a person is ticklish, he/she laughs when sb touches him/her in a sensitive place 怕痒的: Are you ticklish? 你怕痒吗？

tidal
/ˈtaɪdl ||; ˈtaɪdḷ/adj connected with the regular rise and fall of the sea (tides) 与潮汐有关的

ˈtidal wave
noun [C] a very large wave in the sea which destroys things when it reaches the land, and is often caused by movements under the surface of the earth(an earthquake) 潮汐波；海啸 ☞A more technical term is tsunami. 较专门的用语为tsunami。
